<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm"><a href="/wiki/dogge#Middle_English" title="dogge">dogge</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> (whence also <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scots_language" class="extiw" title="w:Scots language">Scots</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="sco"><a href="/wiki/dug#Scots" title="dug">dug</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">dog</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>), from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/dogga#Old_English" title="dogga">dogga</a></i>, <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/docga#Old_English" title="docga">docga</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> of uncertain origin.
</p><p>The original meaning seems to have been a common dog, as opposed to a well-bred one, or something like '<a href="/wiki/cur" title="cur">cur</a>', and perhaps later came to be used for stocky dogs. Possibly a pet-form diminutive with suffix <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/-ga#Old_English" title="-ga">-ga</a></i> (compare <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/frocga#Old_English" title="frocga">frocga</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">frog</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/Reconstruction:Old_English/picga" title="Reconstruction:Old English/picga">*picga</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">pig</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>), appended to a base <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconstruction:Old_English/dog-&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Reconstruction:Old English/dog- (page does not exist)">*dog-</a></i>, <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconstruction:Old_English/doc-&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Reconstruction:Old English/doc- (page does not exist)">*doc-</a></i> of unclear origin and meaning. One possibility is <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/dox#Old_English" title="dox">dox</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">dark, swarthy</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> (compare <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/frocga#Old_English" title="frocga">frocga</a></i> from <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/frox#Old_English" title="frox">frox</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Another proposal is that it derives from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-West_Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-West Germanic language">Proto-West Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gmw-pro"><a href="/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-West_Germanic/dugan" title="Reconstruction:Proto-West Germanic/dugan">*dugan</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to be suitable</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, the origin of <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/dugan#Old_English" title="dugan">dugan</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to be good, worthy, useful</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/dow#English" title="dow">dow</a></i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de"><a href="/wiki/taugen#German" title="taugen">taugen</a></i>. The theory goes that it could have been an epithet for dogs, commonly used by children, meaning "good/useful animal."<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 14th-century England, <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/hound#English" title="hound">hound</a></i> (from Old English <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/hund#Old_English" title="hund">hund</a></i>) was the general word for all domestic canines, and <i>dog</i> referred to a subtype resembling the modern mastiff and bulldog.<sup id="cite_ref-dog_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dog-6">[6]</a></sup> By the 16th century, <i>dog</i> had become the general word, and <i>hound</i> had begun to refer only to breeds used for <a href="/wiki/hunt" title="hunt">hunting</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> In the 16th century, the word <i>dog</i> was adopted by several continental European languages as their word for <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/mastiff#English" title="mastiff">mastiff</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Noun">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">dog</strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/dogs#English" title="dogs">dogs</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li>A <a href="/wiki/mammal" title="mammal">mammal</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Canis_familiaris" title="Canis familiaris">Canis familiaris</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Canis_lupus_familiaris" title="Canis lupus familiaris">Canis lupus familiaris</a></i>, that has been <a href="/wiki/domesticated" title="domesticated">domesticated</a> for thousands of <a href="/wiki/years" title="years">years</a>, of highly variable appearance due to <a href="/wiki/human" title="human">human</a> breeding.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1918</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W._B._Maxwell" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:W. B. Maxwell">W. B. Maxwell</a>,  chapter 16, in  <cite><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://openlibrary.org/works/OL1097634W">The Mirror and the Lamp</a></cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The preposterous altruism too!<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span>Resist not evil. It is an insane immolation of self—as bad intrinsically as fakirs stabbing themselves or anchorites warping their spines in caves scarcely large enough for a fair-sized <b>dog</b>.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1963</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Margery_Allingham" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Margery Allingham">Margery Allingham</a>,  chapter 19, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_China_Governess" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The China Governess">The China Governess</a></cite>‎<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://openlibrary.org/works/OL2004261W">[4]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">When Timothy and Julia hurried up the staircase to the bedroom floor, where a considerable commotion was taking place, Tim took Barry Leach with him.&nbsp;<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span>. The captive made no resistance and came not only quietly but in a series of eager little rushes like a timid <b>dog</b> on a choke chain.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul>
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">The <b>dog</b> barked all night long.</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li>Any member of the Family <a href="/wiki/Canidae" title="Canidae">Canidae</a>, including domestic dogs, wolves, coyotes, jackals, foxes, and their relatives <span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">extant and extinct</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span>; <a href="/wiki/canid" title="canid">canid</a>.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1989</b>,  John L. Gittleman,  <cite>Carnivore Behavior, Ecology, and Evolution</cite>, page 561:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">This includes the development of hyena-like bone crushers (<i>Osteoborus</i> and <i>Borophagus</i>), a large bone-crushing hunting <b>dog</b> (<i>Aelurodon</i>), and another borophagine frugivorous <b>dog</b> (<i>Carpocyon</i>).</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">often <a href="/wiki/Appendix:English_nouns#Attributive" title="Appendix:English nouns">attributive</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A male dog, <a href="/wiki/wolf" title="wolf">wolf</a> or <a href="/wiki/fox" title="fox">fox</a>, as opposed to a <a href="/wiki/bitch" title="bitch">bitch</a> or <a href="/wiki/vixen" title="vixen">vixen</a>.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><b>1928</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siegfried_Sassoon" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Siegfried Sassoon">Siegfried Sassoon</a>, <i>Memoirs of a Fox-Hunting Man</i>, Penguin 2013, page 149:
<dl><dd>Firstly, he was there to encourage and assist the hounds (a scratch pack – mostly <b>dog</b>-hounds drafted from fox-hound kennels because they were over-sized) […].</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#slang" title="Appendix:Glossary">slang</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="/wiki/derogatory" title="derogatory">derogatory</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A <a href="/wiki/dull" title="dull">dull</a>, <a href="/wiki/unattractive" title="unattractive">unattractive</a> <a href="/wiki/girl" title="girl">girl</a> or <a href="/wiki/woman" title="woman">woman</a>.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">She’s a real <b>dog</b>.</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#slang" title="Appendix:Glossary">slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A <a href="/wiki/man" title="man">man</a> (derived from definition 2).
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">You lucky <b>dog</b>!</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#slang" title="Appendix:Glossary">slang</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="/wiki/derogatory" title="derogatory">derogatory</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A <a href="/wiki/coward" title="coward">coward</a>.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">Come back and fight, you <b>dogs</b>!</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/derogatory" title="derogatory">derogatory</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Someone who is morally reprehensible.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">You dirty <b>dog</b>.</i></div></dd></dl>
<ul style="display: none;"><li><b>1599</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Greene_(dramatist)" class="extiw" title="w:Robert Greene (dramatist)">Robert Greene</a>, <i>Alphonsus, King of Aragon</i> (1599). Act 3.
<dl><dd>Blasphemous <b>dog</b>, I wonder that the earth&nbsp;/ Doth cease from renting vnderneath thy feete,&nbsp;/ To swallow vp those cankred corpes of thine.</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1611</b>,  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bible" class="extiw" title="w:Bible">The Holy Bible,<span class="q-hellip-sp">&nbsp;</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="Conteyning the Old Testament, and the New. Appointed to be Read in Churches.">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></a></cite> (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_James_Version" class="extiw" title="w:King James Version">King James Version</a>), London: <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="Imprinted at London by">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Barker_(printer)" class="extiw" title="w:Robert Barker (printer)">Robert Barker</a>,<span class="q-hellip-sp">&nbsp;</span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="printer to the Kings Most Excellent Maiestie.">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/964384981">964384981</a></small>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Books_of_Kings" class="extiw" title="w:Books of Kings">2 Kings</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/Bible1611/Binder1#page/n483/mode/1up">8:13</a>, column 1:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">And Hazael said ſaid, But what, <i>is</i> thy ſeruant a <b>dogge</b>, that he ſhould doe this great thing?</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1887</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H._Rider_Haggard" class="extiw" title="w:H. Rider Haggard">H. Rider Haggard</a>,  <cite>She: A History of Adventure</cite>‎<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/3155/3155-0.txt">[5]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">[A]t last Mahomed's stood straight up upon its vertebræ, and glared at me through its empty eyeholes, and cursed me with its grinning jaws, because I, a <b>dog</b> of a Christian, disturbed the last sleep of a true believer.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#slang" title="Appendix:Glossary">slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A sexually aggressive man.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2005</b>,  Jordan Houston, Darnell Carlton, Paul Beauregard, Premro Smith, Marlon Goodwin, David Brown, and Willie Hutchinson (lyrics),  “Stay Fly”, in  <cite>Most Known Unknown</cite>‎<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://genius.com/Three-6-mafia-stay-fly-lyrics">[6]</a></sup>, Sony BMG, performed by Three 6 Mafia (featuring Young Buck, 8 Ball, and MJG):</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">DJ Paul is a <b>dog</b>; one you do not trust.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>Any of various mechanical devices for holding, gripping, or fastening something, particularly with a tooth-like projection.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2009</b>,  ForestWorks,  <cite>Chainsaw Operator's Manual</cite>, page 41:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Whenever possible, let the tree support the weight of the chainsaw. Pivot the saw, using the saw's <b>dogs</b> (spikes) as a fulcrum.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="maintenance-line" style="color: #777777;">(Can we <a href="/wiki/Wiktionary:Requests_for_cleanup#dog" title="Wiktionary:Requests for cleanup">clean up</a><sup class="plainlinks">(<a class="external text" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/w/index.php?title=Wiktionary:Requests_for_cleanup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=new&amp;preloadtitle=%5B%5Bdog%5D%5D">+</a>)</sup> this sense?)</span> A <a href="/wiki/click" title="click">click</a> or <a href="/wiki/pallet" title="pallet">pallet</a> adapted to engage the teeth of a ratchet-wheel, to restrain the back action; a click or pawl. (See also: <a href="/wiki/ratchet" title="ratchet">ratchet</a>, <a href="/wiki/windlass" title="windlass">windlass</a>)</li>
<li>A metal support for <a href="/wiki/log" title="log">logs</a> in a fireplace.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">The <b>dogs</b> were too hot to touch.</i></div></dd></dl>
<ul style="display: none;"><li><b>1902</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Conan_Doyle" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Arthur Conan Doyle">Arthur Conan Doyle</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/The_Hound_of_the_Baskervilles" class="extiw" title="s:The Hound of the Baskervilles">The Hound of the Baskervilles</a></i>
<dl><dd>In the great old-fashioned fireplace behind the high iron <b>dogs</b> a log-fire crackled and snapped.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/cartomancy" title="cartomancy">cartomancy</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The eighteenth <a href="/wiki/Lenormand" title="Lenormand">Lenormand</a> card.</li>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/hot_dog" title="hot dog">hot dog</a>.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1994</b> July 21,  Faye Fiore,  “Congress relishes another franking privilege: Meat lobby puts on the dog with exclusive luncheon for lawmakers – experts on pork”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></cite>‎<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://articles.latimes.com/1994-07-21/news/mn-18335_1_hot-dog">[7]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Congressmen gleefully wolfed down every imaginable version of the hot dog&nbsp;– smoked kielbasas, jumbo grillers, Big &amp; Juicy's, kosher <b>dogs</b> and spiced <b>dogs</b> <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/poker" title="poker">poker</a> <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#slang" title="Appendix:Glossary">slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <a href="/wiki/underdog" title="underdog">Underdog</a>.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#slang" title="Appendix:Glossary">slang</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> almost always in the <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#plural" title="Appendix:Glossary">plural</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <a href="/wiki/foot" title="foot">Foot</a>.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">My <b>dogs</b> are barking!</i> ― <span class="e-translation">My feet hurt!</span></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Cockney_rhyming_slang" title="Cockney rhyming slang">Cockney rhyming slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> (from "dog and bone") <a href="/wiki/phone" title="phone">Phone</a> or <a href="/wiki/mobile_phone" title="mobile phone">mobile phone</a>.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">My <b>dog</b> is dead.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">My mobile-phone battery has run out of charge and is no longer able to function.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li>
<li>One of the <a href="/wiki/cone" title="cone">cones</a> used to divide up a <a href="/wiki/racetrack" title="racetrack">racetrack</a> when training horses.</li>
<li><span class="form-of-definition use-with-mention">shortened form of <span class="form-of-definition-link"><i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/dog_meat#English" title="dog meat">dog meat</a></i></span></span>.

<dl><dd><i>That modification turned his Dodge hemi into a <b>dog</b>.</i></dd></dl>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Verb">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">dog</strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3|s|pres-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/dogs#English" title="dogs">dogs</a></b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres|ptcp-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/dogging#English" title="dogging">dogging</a></b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past|and|past|ptcp-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/dogged#English" title="dogged">dogged</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#transitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">transitive</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To pursue with the intent to catch.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#transitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">transitive</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To follow in an annoying or harassing way.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><dl><dd><i>The woman cursed him so that trouble would <b>dog</b> his every step.</i></dd></dl>
<ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1749</b>,  Henry Fielding,  <cite>The History of Tom Jones, a Foundling</cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en"><span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> they were discovered in a very improper manner by the husband of the gypsy, who, from jealousy it seems, had kept a watchful eye over his wife, and had <b>dogged</b> her to the place, where he found her in the arms of her gallant.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2012</b> January 1,  Michael Riordan,  “Tackling Infinity”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Scientist" class="extiw" title="w:American Scientist">American Scientist</a></cite>‎<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.americanscientist.org/bookshelf/pub/tackling-infinity">[8]</a></sup>, volume 100, number 1, page 86:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Some of the most beautiful and thus appealing physical theories, including quantum electrodynamics and quantum gravity, have been <b>dogged</b> for decades by infinities that erupt when theorists try to prod their calculations into new domains. Getting rid of these nagging infinities has probably occupied far more effort than was spent in originating the theories.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2012</b> May 9,  Jonathan Wilson,  “Europa League: Radamel Falcao's Atlético Madrid rout Athletic Bilbao”, in  <cite>the Guardian</cite>‎<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.guardian.co.uk/football/2012/may/09/atletico-madrid-athletic-bilbao-europa-league">[9]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">But this is not an Athletic that ever looks comfortable at the back – a criticism that has often <b>dogged</b> Marcelo Bielsa's sides.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#transitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">transitive</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="/wiki/nautical" title="nautical">nautical</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To fasten a <a href="/wiki/hatch" title="hatch">hatch</a> securely.
<dl><dd><i>It is very important to <b>dog</b> down these hatches...</i></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#intransitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">intransitive</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> emerging usage in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Britain" class="extiw" title="w:Great Britain">Britain</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To watch, or participate, in sexual activity in a public place.
<dl><dd><i>I admit that I like to <b>dog</b> at my local country park.</i></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#intransitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">intransitive</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#transitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">transitive</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To intentionally restrict one's productivity as employee; to work at the slowest rate that goes unpunished.
<dl><dd><i>A surprise inspection of the night shift found that some workers were <b>dogging</b> it.</i></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#transitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">transitive</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To <a href="/wiki/criticize" title="criticize">criticize</a>.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1999</b> March 30,  “Shakedown”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JAG_(TV_series)" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:JAG (TV series)">JAG</a></cite>, season 4, episode 18, CBS:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harmon_Rabb" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Harmon Rabb">Harmon Rabb</a> (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_James_Elliott" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:David James Elliott">David James Elliott</a>): Are you <b>dogging</b> Harm's special meatless meatloaf?<br> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sarah_MacKenzie" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Sarah MacKenzie">Sarah MacKenzie</a> (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catherine_Bell_(actress)" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Catherine Bell (actress)">Catherine Bell</a>): Let's put it this way. If you were to make the Harmon Special on this ship, they'd have to unload it with the toxic waste.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#transitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">transitive</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="/wiki/military" title="military">military</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To <a href="/wiki/divide" title="divide">divide</a> (a <a href="/wiki/watch" title="watch">watch</a>) with a <a href="/wiki/comrade" title="comrade">comrade</a>.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><b>1902</b>, Winfield Scott Schley, <i>Record of Proceedings of a Court of Inquiry</i>
<dl><dd>A. We never stood 4 to 8 p.m. watches, sir. We <b>dogged</b> our watches.<br>Q. I suppose that is 6 to 8 p.m., then; it is a little indistinct. I mean the second dog watch.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>2015</b>, Tom Vetter, <i>30,000 Leagues Undersea</i>
<dl><dd>Meanwhile, we <b>dogged</b> the watch sections so that both halves of the crew could fetch full sea bags of uniforms and gear <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms_2">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Synonyms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">to pursue with intent to catch</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span><span class="ib-colon sense-qualifier-colon">:</span> <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/chase#English" title="chase">chase</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/chase_after#English" title="chase after">chase after</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/go_after#English" title="go after">go after</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/pursue#English" title="pursue">pursue</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/tag#English" title="tag">tag</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/tail#English" title="tail">tail</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/track#English" title="track">track</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/trail#English" title="trail">trail</a></span></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">to restrict one's productivity</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span><span class="ib-colon sense-qualifier-colon">:</span> <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/soldier#English" title="soldier">soldier</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/goldbrick#English" title="goldbrick">goldbrick</a></span></li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Danish">Danish</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Danish">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_3">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Danish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Old Danish language">Old Danish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="gmq-oda"><a href="/wiki/dogh#Old_Danish" title="dogh">dogh</a></i>, which was borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Low_German" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Low German">Middle Low German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="gml"><a href="/wiki/doch#Middle_Low_German" title="doch">doch</a></i>, ultimately from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro"><a href="/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-Germanic/%C3%BEauh" title="Reconstruction:Proto-Germanic/þauh">*þauh</a></i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adverb">Adverb</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Adverb">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="da">dog</strong>
</p>
<ol><li><a href="/wiki/however" title="however">however</a>
<dl><dd>Det er <b>dog</b> ikke sikkert, at de taler sandt.
<dl><dd>It is, <b>however</b>, not certain that they are telling the truth.</dd></dl></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="use-with-mention">Conveying impressedness, emotional affectation, bewilderment.</span>
<dl><dd>Hvor er den hund <b>dog</b> nuttet!
<dl><dd>How cute that dog is!</dd></dl></dd>
<dd>Sikke dramatisk du <b>dog</b> kan fremstille sagen!
<dl><dd>How dramatically you can present the matter!</dd></dl></dd></dl></li></ol>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_4">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_2">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Noun">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl">dog</strong>&nbsp;<span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href="/wiki/doggen#Dutch" title="doggen">doggen</a></b>, <i><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#diminutive" title="Appendix:Glossary">diminutive</a></i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href="/wiki/dogje#Dutch" title="dogje">dogje</a></b>&nbsp;<span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li>A large <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/dog#English" title="dog">dog</a></span>, especially one of certain <a href="/wiki/breed" title="breed">breeds</a>.</li></ol>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mbabaram">Mbabaram</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Mbabaram">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_6">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From <i class="Latn mention" lang="vmb"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconstruction:Mbabaram/dwog(a)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Reconstruction:Mbabaram/dwog(a) (page does not exist)">*dwog(a)</a></i>, from <i class="Latn mention" lang="vmb"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconstruction:Mbabaram/udwoga&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Reconstruction:Mbabaram/udwoga (page does not exist)">*udwoga</a></i>, from <i class="Latn mention" lang="vmb"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconstruction:Mbabaram/gudwaga&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Reconstruction:Mbabaram/gudwaga (page does not exist)">*gudwaga</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pama%E2%80%93Nyungan_languages" class="extiw" title="w:Pama–Nyungan languages">Proto-Pama-Nyungan</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="aus-pam-pro"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconstruction:Proto-Pama-Nyungan/gudaga&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Reconstruction:Proto-Pama-Nyungan/gudaga (page does not exist)">*gudaga</a></i>. Related to <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dyirbal_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dyirbal language">Dyirbal</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dbl"><a href="/wiki/guda#Dyirbal" title="guda">guda</a></i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yidiny_language" class="extiw" title="w:Yidiny language">Yidiny</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="yii"><a href="/wiki/gudaga#Yidiny" title="gudaga">gudaga</a></i>. Not related to <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/dog#English" title="dog">dog</a></i>; it is a <a href="/wiki/false_cognate" title="false cognate">false cognate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-anderson_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anderson-10">[2]</a></sup>
</p>
